		function setCookie(c_name,value,exdays) {
			var exdate=new Date();
			exdate.setDate(exdate.getDate() + exdays);
			var c_value=escape(value) + ((exdays==null) ? "" : "; expires="+exdate.toUTCString());
			document.cookie=c_name + "=" + c_value;
		}
		
		function getCookie(c_name) {
			var i,x,y,ARRcookies=document.cookie.split(";");
			for (i=0;i<ARRcookies.length;i++) {
			  	x=ARRcookies[i].substr(0,ARRcookies[i].indexOf("="));
			  	y=ARRcookies[i].substr(ARRcookies[i].indexOf("=")+1);
			  	x=x.replace(/^\s+|\s+$/g,"");
			  	if (x==c_name) {
					return unescape(y);
				}
		    }

		<p id="breadcrumbs"><span xmlns:v="http://rdf.data-vocabulary.org/#"><span typeof="v:Breadcrumb"><a href="http://paultan.org" rel="v:url" property="v:title">Home</a></span> &raquo; <span typeof="v:Breadcrumb"><a href="http://paultan.org/topics/global-car-launches/" rel="v:url" property="v:title">Global Car Launches</a></span> &raquo; <span typeof="v:Breadcrumb"><strong class="breadcrumb_last" property="v:title">2014 Mazda 3 5-door hatchback makes world debut</strong></span></span></p></span>
		
		<article class="single">
			<h1 class="xlarge">2014 Mazda 3 5-door hatchback makes world debut</h1>
			<p class="postmetadata">
				<span class="category">In <a href="http://paultan.org/topics/cars/" title="View all posts in Cars" rel="category tag">Cars</a>, <a href="http://paultan.org/topics/global-car-launches/" title="View all posts in Global Car Launches" rel="category tag">Global Car Launches</a>, <a href="http://paultan.org/topics/intl-news/" title="View all posts in International News" rel="category tag">International News</a>, <a href="http://paultan.org/topics/cars/mazda/" title="View all posts in Mazda" rel="category tag">Mazda</a></span>				 / <span class="author">By <a href="http://paultan.org/author/paul/" title="Posts by Paul Tan" rel="author">Paul Tan</a></span>				 / <time datetime="2013-06-26" pubdate>26 June 2013 11:48 pm</time>				 / <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/#comments" title="Comment on 2014 Mazda 3 5-door hatchback makes world debut">174 comments</a>			</p>

<div style="margin-top: 5px; background-color: #f9f9f9; padding: 5px 0 5px 8px; border-top: 1px solid #dddddd; border-bottom: 1px solid #dddddd">
<div class="fb-like" data-href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/" data-send="true" data-layout="button_count" data-width="150" data-show-faces="false" style="vertical-align:top;zoom:1;*display:inline"></div>
<div class="g-plusone" data-size="medium" data-href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/"></div>
</div>			










			<div class="post-content">
				<p><a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/2014-mazda3-0005/" rel="attachment wp-att-183081"><img src="http://s5.paultan.org/image/2013/06/2014-mazda3-0005-630x322.jpg" alt="2014-mazda3-0005" width="630" height="322" class="aligncenter size-medium wp-image-183081" /></a></p>
<p>The next-generation Mazda 3 is here, revealed as a five-door hatchback first &#8211; the car was launched in five countries at a go, with Melbourne hosting the global reveal ahead of launch events in New York, London, St Petersburg and Istanbul. The new car shares its handsome looks with larger sibling <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/03/20/mazda-6-launch/" target="_blank">Mazda 6</a>, and the sedan version that will probably come later will look even more like a mini <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/03/20/mazda-6-launch/" target="_blank">Mazda 6</a>.</p>
<p>The new Mazda 3 is on average about 60 kg lighter than <a href="http://paultan.org/2011/03/02/mazda3-ckd-launched-starts-from-rm99k-for-1-6-sedan/" target="_blank">its predecessor</a>, despite being a larger car. Its wheelbase has grown 60 mm to 2,700 mm, and it&#8217;s now 4,465 mm long, 1,795 mm wide and 1,450 mm tall, which represents a growth of about 5 mm, 40 mm and 20 mm respectively. </p>
<p>It&#8217;s worth noting that the 2014 Mazda 3 now has a longer wheelbase than the <a href="http://paultan.org/2012/09/13/ford-focus-3rd-gen-c346-debuts-rm116k-rm129k/" target="_blank">Mk3 Ford Focus</a> &#8211; other than the <a href="http://paultan.org/2010/04/05/mazda-2-launched-sedan-and-hatchback-rm80k-to-rm85k/" target="_blank">Mazda 2</a> and the <a href="http://paultan.org/2012/09/11/mazda-bt-50-truck-full-live-gallery-specs-and-prices/" target="_blank">BT-50 truck</a>, there&#8217;s not much platform sharing with Ford going on any longer. The car rides on MacPherson struts at the front and a multi-link suspension at the rear.</p>
<p><a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/2014-mazda3-0004/" rel="attachment wp-att-183080"><img src="http://s5.paultan.org/image/2013/06/2014-mazda3-0004-630x401.jpg" alt="2014-mazda3-0004" width="630" height="401" class="aligncenter size-medium wp-image-183080" /></a></p>
<p>Five engines have been announced at launch &#8211; a new 1.5 litre SkyActiv-G engine, two different tunes for the 2.0 litre SkyActiv-G engine, a 2.5 litre SkyActiv-G engine, and a single 2.2 litre SkyActiv-D diesel motor. </p>
<p>The new 1.5 litre SkyActiv-G slots in between the 1.3 litre and 2.0 litre versions and outputs 100 PS at 6,000 rpm and 150 Nm of torque at 4,000 rpm with direct injection and a compression ratio of 14.0:1.</p>
<p>The lower powered version of the 2.0 litre SkyActiv-G engine produces 120 PS and 210 Nm of torque, curiously low power for a 2.0 litre engine. It&#8217;s obviously detuned for fuel economy and emissions purposes because the high power version of the engine with the i-ELOOP system produces 165 PS and 210 Nm. Both engines have direct injection and run a 14.0:1 compression ratio.</p>
<p><a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/2014-mazda3-0013/" rel="attachment wp-att-183089"><img src="http://s4.paultan.org/image/2013/06/2014-mazda3-0013-630x420.jpg" alt="2014-mazda3-0013" width="630" height="420" class="aligncenter size-medium wp-image-183089" /></a></p>
<p>The SkyActiv-D 2.2 litre engine produces 150 PS at 4,500 rpm and is the most torquey of the lot &#8211; 380 Nm at 1,800 rpm. All four engines can be had with a six-speed manual transmission. The low-power 2.0 as well as the 2.2 diesel can be had with a six-speed automatic. The final engine is the 2.5 litre SkyActiv-G, which is likely to be quite similiar to the one in the Mazda 6.</p>
<p>Mazda also announced that the Mazda 3 sedan will be coming and will also be available with a petrol electric hybrid powertrain &#8211; if it&#8217;s mated to a 2.0 litre and below engine capacity, perhaps we might see it introduced at a very good price in Malaysia?</p>
<p>What do you think of the new Mazda 3? Like what you see?</p>

After dabbling for years in the IT industry, Paul Tan initially began this site as a general blog covering various topics of personal interest. With an increasing number of readers paying rapt attention to the motoring stories, one thing led to another and the rest, as they say, is history. An avid electronic gadget aficionado as well as big-time coffee lover, he's also the executive producer of the Driven motoring TV programme.

			 <strong><cite class="fn">4G63T DSM</cite></strong>

			on <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/#comment-1371207">Jun 27, 2013 </a>
			at <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/#comment-1371207">12:40 pm</a>
			

			
					</div>
      </div>

      <div style=""><p>The difference in road tax is not really significant if you split the difference into months. BTW, both power units are GDI. As someone pointed out. Read the article again.</p>
<p>Don&#8217;t just look at numbers. They only tell half the story. Test drive the car when it comes out. </p>
<p>The general car buying public has been loong hoodwinked into only taking hp numbers as doctrine. (Like camera buyers looking for megapixels)</p>
<p>How well a car drives (or if it feels underpowered) is dependent on a lot of other factors, such as gearing, vehicle weight and ignition and valve timing. This is the basis of Mazda&#8217;s Skyactive philosophy. </p>
<p>My guess is the 120hp unit will offer much better drivability in-city with exceptional fuel economy. And you don&#8217;t have to rev the headbolts off it to get meaningful power. You have to understand that HP is a calculated figure from power over time. Which means, the higher you rev an engine , the more HP it makes. Bringing down the peak power RPM will lower HP but will also make the engine more responsive at lower rpm. </p>
<p>I personally prefer the japanese to be more active in force feeding their engines, but to each their own.</p>
<p>With 60kg saved, those of us in drag racing will typically equate that to about the equivalent of an additional 10hp &#8220;gain&#8221; in power.</p>
</div><div class="CommentRating">Well-loved. Like or Dislike: <img style="padding: 0px; margin: 0px; border: none; cursor: pointer;" onmouseover="this.width=this.width*1.3" onmouseout="this.width=this.width/1.2" id="up-1371207" src="http://s5.paultan.org/wp-content/plugins/comment-rating-redis/images/1_14_up.png" alt="Thumb up" onclick="javascript:ckratingKarma('1371207', 'add', 'paultan.org/wp-content/plugins/comment-rating-redis/', '1_14_');" title="Thumb up" /> <span id="karma-1371207-up" style="font-size:12px; color:#009933;">64</span>&nbsp;<img style="padding: 0px; margin: 0px; border: none; cursor: pointer;" onmouseover="this.width=this.width*1.3" onmouseout="this.width=this.width/1.2" id="down-1371207" src="http://s5.paultan.org/wp-content/plugins/comment-rating-redis/images/1_14_down.png" alt="Thumb down" onclick="javascript:ckratingKarma('1371207', 'subtract', 'paultan.org/wp-content/plugins/comment-rating-redis/', '1_14_')" title="Thumb down" /> <span id="karma-1371207-down" style="font-size:12px; color:#990033;">1</span></div>            <!-- <br /> -->

      </div>

      <p>All it needs is the 2.3L DISI turbo engine producing a healthy 340hp to compete with the M135i, S3, A45 AMG, and the upcoming Subaru WRX STi.</p>

<p>as such, IMHO, Mazda is clearly more refined compared to Mitsubishi, but the latter is a bit brash and quite a lot fun too &#8211; minus the current Mirage, haha.</p>

   <li class="comment even depth-2" id="li-comment-1371641">
	<div id="comment-1371641" class="commbody">
	 <div class="commleft">
		  <div class="comment-author vcard">
		  

		  
			 <img alt='' src='http://paultan.org/wp-content/glc_cache/1320937301a4c2f5e5e04e3dd2fc4e8b-80.jpg' class='avatar avatar-80 photo' height='80' width='80' />
			 <strong><cite class="fn">Moores</cite></strong>

			on <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/#comment-1371641">Jun 27, 2013 </a>
			at <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/#comment-1371641">4:48 pm</a>
			

			
					</div>
      </div>

      <p>Again and again, why do we always only care about hp so much?? To achieve a good &#8216;day to day&#8217; driving one really have to look at the torque and not hp. Torque is the one that pulls your car from stationary and that&#8217;s what really matters to most of us, acceleration. Hp on the other hand will come in handy if you want to reach higher speed. Now, how many of us are pushing our car to the max speed everyday?? Secondly, beside torque (not hp), one should look at how good the transmission do their work. Remember transmission is the one that give force to the wheels not the engine. Thirdly, weight of the car. A car with more horsepower but heavier or a car with less horsepower but lighter? You decide.</p>

   <li class="comment even depth-2" id="li-comment-1371715">
	<div id="comment-1371715" class="commbody">
	 <div class="commleft">
		  <div class="comment-author vcard">
		  

		  
			 <img alt='' src='http://paultan.org/wp-content/glc_cache/637fa1594d63d5364a938e9fd258be40-80.jpg' class='avatar avatar-80 photo' height='80' width='80' />
			 <strong><cite class="fn">lampard</cite></strong>

			on <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/#comment-1371715">Jun 27, 2013 </a>
			at <a href="http://paultan.org/2013/06/26/2014-mazda3-hatchback/#comment-1371715">5:24 pm</a>
			

			
					</div>
      </div>

      <p>FC FC FC FC&#8230;..</p>
<p>Well, skyactiv seems to mock up turbocharged engine. Lower displacement, higher torque. This car (low powered version) might have top speed of only 190km/h as the hp is quite low. If you want the higher top speed, choose the high powered version, but prolly its FC of the city usage is higher than the low powered one.</p>
<p>Detuning the GDI engine to lower compression ratio so that it&#8217;ll be able to accept ron95 fuel might decrease its performance, but I believe it&#8217;s just about 5% decrease from the original version (compression ratio 14.0:1). So it&#8217;ll be about 200nm, still not bad. (For record preve turbo has 205nm) </p>
<p>Last, have to look at the torque at low rpm. That would be essential for city driving FC and of course the pick up from standstill. If I&#8217;m not mistaken it reaches quite high number of torque at low 2,000rpm. That&#8217;s quite good actually.</p>
<p>Have to test it yourself later.</p>

      <p>This car isn&#8217;t aimed for you. Mazda has the sporty philosophy and they back that up. That&#8217;s what I like about them. They aren&#8217;t trying to﻿ be everything for everyone. They go after a certain kind of driver. one who likes to drive and driver engagement. yes the downside of a sporty ride is you feel a lot. People who like disconnected and cushy rides buy a T or H. Not bashing you just saying different strokes for different folks. Cheers.</p>
